Very low end golf course that plays between an executive course and a championship course in distance. The greens are poorly engineered with way too much slope, making for many approach shots, putts, and chips to role off the green even when executed relatively well. The price is economical, there is a driving range and practice putting green. I recommend it for the budgetary golfer who is not too serious about their game.< /Review>

It is a fine enough course.  It is short, so if you need work with your wedges go there.  If I want to get a quick round in it is easily done here.  Staff is friendly.

I do have a couple of issues that trouble me.  There aren‚Äôt kid prices.  My six year old loves golf and wants to play with me every time I go.  I would like to have him go more often.  It seems a little ridiculous to pay the adult price for a six year old, really $22 for a six year old.  It seems that as a good business strategy kids play for free or a nominal price.  It would get them interested in the game of golf and become future clients as they age.  Speaking for me I know I would go more often because I could bring my son along.  I hear the argument well kids will damage the ground and the greens, but maybe it is just my experience but I take and make more divots and spike marks than my kids.
Also, prices went up $2 this year.  I could go to surrounding courses and pay a couple more bucks and play a 71 par course.  This is something that keeps me from playing more often.<//Text>

{'time': 1520710855566, 'text': 'Mr. Syvertsen, just to let you know we have raised our prices 1 time in the last 12 years. We went up $1 dollar in 2016 to help with the increase in general operation costs that are out of our control, but at the same time added a super twilight rate, military discounts and junior programs.  Addressing the slow play, would you let us know what day you played and who told you that you could not play through slow players? Our records indicate the average time it takes to play our course is under 3 hours, and management would never have an issue with a slower group allowing groups to play through. It is very typical that our staff will even inform slower groups to let others play through. We are also working to recover from the flood we sustained last year rebuilding the back 9, so course conditions are on the way back up and we look forward to the growing season when we can really make more improvements.\n\nThank you for your feedback, we continue to look for ways to improve the offering we provide to the community.'}<//response>
< Text>
UPDATE!!
I had previously posted a critical review but recent changes at the course prompted this edit.

We heard Jacktone Golf had made improvements so we decided to give it a try again.  There has been a HUGE IMPROVEMENT in the course.  The brush is cleared, the fairways are mowed, certain trees removed, and last but not least, the greens are now in really good shape.  The bare spots on the greens are a thing of the past and they are now being regularly maintained.  Also, the middle-aged guy at the desk who gave us grief appears to be gone and the cordial young ladies have returned.  As for the fees, perhaps we confused a twilight rate with regular play.  All is forgiven.  I now highly recommend Jacktone Golf for a quick, fun course to sharpen your short iron skills.< /Text>

<Resp>None</Resp>< Text>
(Translated by Google) It is one of the Catholic churches in the Parish of San Jose, and the current church seems to have been built in 1963. The Food & Fan Festa was held on October 5.6.7 and many people came. There were also stores that reminded me of Japanese festivals such as freefalls and coasters, such as screaming and shooting. Besides food such as hamburgers, there were also foreign dishes. I bought a bowl of rice with meat and vegetables on it. The rice inside was not completely cooked and the core remained.

<username>juma love< /username><Text>Talk about a FAT sandwich.  I had the Turkey Reuben, which was served hot!  Loved my first experience here. 104699402925738896219< /user_id>
<user_name>Daniel Yang<//user_name><time>1540493535775<//time>< Rate>
3</Rate>
< review>
This is not just a review on the food, but my overall vibe that I got from there.  I waited a month to write this because I didn't want to post a gut reaction to my experience and write something weird.  I ordered a pastrami on rye with Russian dressing, and potato salad.  I sat at the single table by the kitchen, while the rest of the crowd was at the front dining area.  During my time by the kitchen, I felt uncomfortable because the owner was very condescending to his employees.  Lots of snide remarks, lots of unreasonable requests.  I felt bad for those 2 guys working there.  They were doing everything they could , saying "yes sir" to every request and it wasn't good enough.  After I ate my food, the owner made his rounds making sure everyone was pleased.  He himself is very friendly to the customers, but in the kitchen behind the counter it wasn't the same guy.  You can tell what kind of person someone is by the way they treat their employees.  All that said ,  the food was fantastic. The pastrami was closer to a high end 12 hour smoked brisket in texture and flavor than what I would consider transitional pastrami.  Different, but delicious.  As you can see in my pics, portions are huge. I was full after half.  Food is a 4+.  Awkward vibe made it a 3.< /review>

I lived in New York for 8 years. At one point I rented a car and drove to pick up every famous chicken soup in Manhattan and Brooklyn, so I could once and for all settle it for myself. I think I got 6 different soups. Katz turned out to be the winner in my book.
I've since moved to la and forgotten all about the concept a good New York deli. Then one day sick as a dog I needed soup! New York famous deli was the closest spot and so I gave it a shot. Oh man. This is truly the best chicken soup I've tried in Los Angeles OR New York. I get it every time I'm under the weather and it does wonders. I should go here more when I'm healthy. From what I hear everything else is just as good. Plus it's run by a great New Yorker, Jimmy.< /review>

<rating>4< /rating><review>Pretty cool how there's a korean market in Glendale. It closes at 10:55 pm by the way. Not 11pm. Not 10:30pm. I came around 10:30 pm, and all the banchan was closed off T_T

This was the only time I've gone, so I will be back during normal market hours to see if it's livelier. I would say that this market has one of the cheapest produce and meat in that area compared to the American markets like Ralph's and Trader Joes.

This is a VERY korean market, and therefore has the many sauces associated with korean food (SCORE!!).

They also have a lot of sashimi option and cheap uni. However, the uni quality, like that of Korean markets, is subpar- pale yellow and limp. But if you make some pasta sauce from that, you won't be able to taste the difference ;)

I'll be back to score on some banchan.< /review><Date>1418783764863<//Date></record>

When I first went into this offiice, it was quite small, I was greeted, and the staff was friendly. One was busy helping the customer while the other was helping with another customer on the phone checking rates. They informed me that they will be with me as soon as possible. It was a good 10 minute wait, I was expecting for them to ask me if I had a reservation to move the process quicker. The rental process was decent, I think there was another individual working there who was helping another person move the fridge? But no point were taken off because of that, I don't think he had another computer or terminal to help me even if he wanted to. But, when lines got long at Enterprise, I do recall where an agent would walk me out with a couple of keys and inform me which car I would like to rent instead of having me just wait in a long line and to start the paperwork. The selection of the vehicle were limited to 1 of each of the category. It has happened before so I informed them this vehicle is deemed hazardous so I will not accept this, maybe a little eye roll was given to me ... but safety is an issue to my family and I.

I was then given another alternative, which I am sure would have been the same price for a smaller size which is compact even though I paid for the upgrade for midsize which was for a Scion XA in which, I know I am unable to put my pregnant wife and a car seat for my child to sit comfortably.

This is another restaurant that my daughter absolutely loves. So from her point of view it's a 5.

From my point of view it's a three because I don't think there's anything particularly healthy or special about the food. I think for the price you can get a lot of food, in fact as much as you want to stuff down your throat. But I prefer to eat food that is health-giving and life-sustaining. I don't think there's anything like that here.

It's a little confusing when you first walk in as to what to do. Should I go pay and then should I get my food or should I just start piling stuff onto a plate? I don't think I saw any signs that let you know what to do either. Usually don't see staff to get halfway down the first line and that's the cashier. The staff is friendly so I have no complaints there. And I do think it's a good value if you just are super hungry and don't have a great concerned over whether the food is necessarily healthy or nutritious. They obviously have a great variety of food and that maybe is the appeal for a lot of people too.<//Text>

The greetings from management are friendly, welcomed & appreciated thank you (please make eye contact with the person or people too). Though the lack of courtesy & attentiveness from the servers is poor.
